  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_66cb6e92-b2ee-41f3-908f-f5b5cf47b248'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer11555143261319531384">Agatha Christie is the most widely published author of all time with her works outsold only by Shakespeare and the Bible. She is regarded by generations of fans as the greatest mystery writer ever, and her novels are read and cherished the world over.<br/><br/>A thriller as well as a puzzler set in a foggy estate in Wales. This mystery opens as a stranger walks away from his ditched</span>
  <span id="freeText11555143261319531384" style="display:none">Agatha Christie is the most widely published author of all time with her works outsold only by Shakespeare and the Bible. She is regarded by generations of fans as the greatest mystery writer ever, and her novels are read and cherished the world over.<br /><br />A thriller as well as a puzzler set in a foggy estate in Wales. This mystery opens as a stranger walks away from his ditched car toward a country manor to find a man murdered and his wife standing over him with a gun. But the woman is dazed and her confession unconvincing. The unexpected guest decides to help her and blame the murder on an intruder. Later, the police discover clues that point to a man who died two years previously and a pandora's box of loves and hates, suspicions and intrigues is opened to the night air.<br /><br />Originally written by Agatha Christie as a play in 1954, now rendered as a novel by Charles Osborne, <i>The Unexpected Guest</i> is a compelling tale of murder and deceit sure to entertain and amuse fans of Christie worldwide.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11555143261319531384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I liked the book, but felt like I would have enjoyed reading the play more. There were too many stage directions in the book, and it became tedious "S<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I liked the book, but felt like I would have enjoyed reading the play more. There were too many stage directions in the book, and it became tedious "Starkwedder crossed the room to the armchair, Laura walked over to the window" that sort of thing seemed kind of clunky.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/898693-someone-recommended-agatha-christie-books">Someone recommended Agatha Christie books for me because I love mysteries, however I like books like Diagnosis Murder/ Monk series. Are her books similar or more gory like James Patterson/Stephen King. It is hard to tell with some of the titles and reviews?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_898693'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F948072.The_Unexpected_Guest">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/898693-someone-recommended-agatha-christie-books">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/898693-someone-recommended-agatha-christie-books">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/36609694-kelly"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1480975752i/36609694._UX100_CR0,40,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/36609694-kelly">Kelly</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Her books are not gory at all, the stories are generally all about the puzzle. Characters are not very complex. These books are basically whodunits, a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Her books are not gory at all, the stories are generally all about the puzzle. Characters are not very complex. These books are basically whodunits, and give the reader a feeling of nostalgia for Britain of the past.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3365921434340544607"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18240860.The_Unexpected_Guest' title='The Unexpected Guest by Charles Osborne' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Unexpected Guest</a> began life as a play by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a>. This is the novelized version written by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5477352.Charles_Osborne' title='Charles Osborne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charles Osborne</a>.<br/><br/>As you read it is obvious that it is derived from a play because the entire novel takes place in one room. Characters arrive and depart from this room, individually or in groups, from one door or another, just as actors would come and go on stage. This does not detract at all from the quality of the writing or the story itself.<br/><br/>Like many Christie novels the mystery is spun out an</span>
  <span id="freeText3365921434340544607" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18240860.The_Unexpected_Guest" title="The Unexpected Guest by Charles Osborne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unexpected Guest</a> began life as a play by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>. This is the novelized version written by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5477352.Charles_Osborne" title="Charles Osborne" rel="nofollow noopener">Charles Osborne</a>.<br /><br />As you read it is obvious that it is derived from a play because the entire novel takes place in one room. Characters arrive and depart from this room, individually or in groups, from one door or another, just as actors would come and go on stage. This does not detract at all from the quality of the writing or the story itself.<br /><br />Like many Christie novels the mystery is spun out and almost everyone was suspected of being the murderer at one point or another. Eventually one of the least likely suspects showed another side to his character and became the guilty party. Until the very last page......<br /><br /> If you like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a> and have not read this yet then do. It is a good one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6694824601794946162">Having read every full length novel by the queen of crime I came across this play that has been adapted into a novel. I started to read this book and very soon I knew I had picked a good book to read, I could easily picture this been played out on a stage and it had the usual twists and turns that any Agatha Christie reader would expect. As with most Christie novels the finger of suspicion moved from character to character as more facts were told.<br/>The novel starts with a stranger running his car </span>
  <span id="freeText6694824601794946162" style="display:none">Having read every full length novel by the queen of crime I came across this play that has been adapted into a novel. I started to read this book and very soon I knew I had picked a good book to read, I could easily picture this been played out on a stage and it had the usual twists and turns that any Agatha Christie reader would expect. As with most Christie novels the finger of suspicion moved from character to character as more facts were told.<br />The novel starts with a stranger running his car into a ditch in dense fog near the South Wales coast, and making his way to an isolated house where he discovers a woman standing over the dead body of her wheelchair-bound husband, gun in her hand. She admits to murder, and the unexpected guest offers to help her concoct a cover story. There is a doubt that the woman, Laura Warwick did not actually commit the murder after-all but why why would she admit guilt. The house is full of suspects and in turn you will suspect all of them.<br />It was good to read one of my all time favourite authors work with this 1958 adapted play.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6694824601794946162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1515267236193971982">Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16346.Spider_s_Web' title='Spider's Web by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spider's Web</a>, <i> The Unexpected Guest</i> is yet another play of Dame <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a>’s that was turned into a novel by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5477352.Charles_Osborne' title='Charles Osborne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charles Osborne</a>. Both of the plays-turned-novels were originally published in 2000 and recently turned into audiobooks; while neither feature Christie’s usual characters of Miss Jane Marple, Hercule Poirot, or Tommy and Tuppence Beresford, both are equally fabulous.<br/><br/>Due to a pea fog, Michael Starkwedder runs his car off the road and arrives at a house, only to find the wheelchair</span>
  <span id="freeText1515267236193971982" style="display:none">Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16346.Spider_s_Web" title="Spider's Web by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Spider's Web</a>, <i> The Unexpected Guest</i> is yet another play of Dame <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>’s that was turned into a novel by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5477352.Charles_Osborne" title="Charles Osborne" rel="nofollow noopener">Charles Osborne</a>. Both of the plays-turned-novels were originally published in 2000 and recently turned into audiobooks; while neither feature Christie’s usual characters of Miss Jane Marple, Hercule Poirot, or Tommy and Tuppence Beresford, both are equally fabulous.<br /><br />Due to a pea fog, Michael Starkwedder runs his car off the road and arrives at a house, only to find the wheelchair-bound Richard Warwick shot in the head and his wife, the beautiful Laura Warwick, holding the gun. She claims to have shot and killed her husband, but Starkwedder begins to doubt her story. Is she innocent and shielding someone, as he thinks, or has he been taken in by a pretty face? Plenty of twists in a rollercoaster of a novel that will keep you guessing to the very, very end. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4777980097780613639">The Unexpected Guest is another play by Agatha Christie that was adapted as a novel Charles Osborne - so in short, it is not that great.<br/> <br/>Of course I am peeved that I ended up with this book because it was advertised as an Agatha Christie novel, and it is not, but I am also astounded Osborne got to write several novelisations at all, and all of them on commission by Christie's estate!<br/> <br/>He has no feel for Christie's characters.<br/> <br/>While I can see that the setting in this novel is a typical Christie co</span>
  <span id="freeText4777980097780613639" style="display:none">The Unexpected Guest is another play by Agatha Christie that was adapted as a novel Charles Osborne - so in short, it is not that great.<br /> <br />Of course I am peeved that I ended up with this book because it was advertised as an Agatha Christie novel, and it is not, but I am also astounded Osborne got to write several novelisations at all, and all of them on commission by Christie's estate!<br /> <br />He has no feel for Christie's characters.<br /> <br />While I can see that the setting in this novel is a typical Christie country house mystery, the main character of Laura Warwick does not strike me as a Christie woman at all.<br /> <br />But maybe I'm just peeved that Audible did not make it clear that this was an Osborne novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4777980097780613639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText15380384357106755684" style="display:none">I commend Charles Osborne for his work on the play The Unexpected Guest, because I can imagine it must be a daunting task to turn the play which entirely occurs in one setting - a study room- into an Agatha Christie novel, who is a master of her work. The book, though understandably rushed, manages to capture all the mystery and surprise which, I’m guessing, the Dame wanted the attendees of the play to experience. Her craftiness was clearly shown in the clever setting and as always she managed to thwart my thought-process quite elaborately.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer3118084967923859615">The plot is incorrect: it's the one for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16346.Spider_s_Web__Agatha_Christie_Collection_' title='Spider's Web (Agatha Christie Collection) by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spider's Web</a>. I guess you could say I read "The Unexpected Guest" as an accident, as I thought I would be reading Spider's Web. However, The Unexpected Guest was a <i>very <b>good</b></i> accident, mind you. The story was fast-paced, had simple and easy-to-read language, and a jaw-dropping ending.<br/><br/>It didn't feature the usual recurring detectives, like Poirot or Marple or Tommy and Tuppence, yet perhaps that's what made this book so intriguing because the inspectors were </span>
  <span id="freeText3118084967923859615" style="display:none">The plot is incorrect: it's the one for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16346.Spider_s_Web__Agatha_Christie_Collection_" title="Spider's Web (Agatha Christie Collection) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Spider's Web</a>. I guess you could say I read "The Unexpected Guest" as an accident, as I thought I would be reading Spider's Web. However, The Unexpected Guest was a <i>very <b>good</b></i> accident, mind you. The story was fast-paced, had simple and easy-to-read language, and a jaw-dropping ending.<br /><br />It didn't feature the usual recurring detectives, like Poirot or Marple or Tommy and Tuppence, yet perhaps that's what made this book so intriguing because the inspectors were characters you haven't been entirely familiar with so you didn't have to give much thought to the things they say. They weren't "super geniuses" with extraordinary mystery-solving brain power.<br /><br />I would have liked a more thorough explanation about the contents of Mrs Warwick Sr's envelope--it may have clued-in readers on the identity of the murderer.<br /><br /><br />But I guess that's why Agatha Christie didn't give an explanation.</span>

<div id="review_152328720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152328720" />
    <a title="Bev" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5082359-bev"><img alt="Bev" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374365942p2/5082359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152328720?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bev" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bev" href="/user/show/5082359-bev">Bev</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312242626" href="/book/show/1626917.The_Unexpected_Guest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=vintage-mystery">vintage-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=mount-tbr-2019">mount-tbr-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=british-mystery">british-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=set-in-wales">set-in-wales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152328720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8370767191744529039">The unexpected guest is Michael Starkwedder who has come to Wales to visit the country of his mother's youth and perhaps buy a house. The night is foggy and he runs his car into a muddy ditch. When he goes for help at the nearest house, he finds that he's not the only unexpected guest there--death has visited the home of Richard and Laura Warwick. The master of the house, Richard, lies dead of a gunshot wound and Laura stands nearby with the gun in her hand. She swears that she has killed her hu</span>
  <span id="freeText8370767191744529039" style="display:none">The unexpected guest is Michael Starkwedder who has come to Wales to visit the country of his mother's youth and perhaps buy a house. The night is foggy and he runs his car into a muddy ditch. When he goes for help at the nearest house, he finds that he's not the only unexpected guest there--death has visited the home of Richard and Laura Warwick. The master of the house, Richard, lies dead of a gunshot wound and Laura stands nearby with the gun in her hand. She swears that she has killed her husband because he was cruel to her and others in the house, but Michael doesn't believe her. He thinks she's covering for someone else and he decides to help her fool the police. They manufacture evidence pointing towards a man who swore vengeance on Richard after he ran over the man's son. (Richard was exonerated of guilt because the nurse who was with him swore he was sober and driving under the speed limit.) But when the police try to track the vengeful MacGregor down, they find that he died some time ago in Canada. <br /><br />So who did it? Did Laura really kill her husband after all. Maybe it was her lover--the man Michael thinks Laura is covering for. As the story goes on, everyone from Richard's mother to his half-brother to his secretary/housekeeper to his valet/male nurse seems to have a motive to do away with the unpleasant man--or at least to shield someone they think did it. So they all look suspicious. The police decide they've found their man/woman in the end...but did they?<br /><br />I'm very tempted to count this for 1954 (for a couple of challenges)--while the novelization was published in 1999, Osborne has, according to Wikipedia, not added one jot or iota to the Christie play. "The novelisation is a straightforward transfer of the stage lines and directions of Christie's script into a written narrative." The book's play roots are pretty apparent, especially when stage directions are worked into the narrative. For example, "He crossed to the french window, held back a curtain, and peered out as though seeking inspiration." But the story itself is worthy of Dame Agatha and the fact that I spotted the killer doesn't detract from that--especially since I just latched onto the person as soon as they came on the scene and didn't really worry about whether clues were pointing that way or not. It would be nice to see the play (or read the script) and see exactly how Christie intended it. ★★★ and 1/2. <br /><br />First posted on my blog <a href="https://myreadersblock.blogspot.com/2019/10/the-unexpected-guest.html" rel="nofollow noopener">My Reader's Block</a>. Please request permission before reposting any review content. Thanks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8370767191744529039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review152328720">

<div id="review_2644708093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2644708093" />
    <a title="Sarah-Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76784705-sarah-grace"><img alt="Sarah-Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605996039p2/76784705.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2644708093?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah-Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah-Grace" href="/user/show/76784705-sarah-grace">Sarah-Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76784705-sarah-grace?shelf=2019-ha-abc-challenge">2019-ha-abc-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76784705-sarah-grace?shelf=scribd">scribd</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2644708093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5354569607574130468">Good story with an unexpected twist, unexpected to me at least.<br/><br/>The story is a novel adaptation of one of Agatha Christie's plays. I enjoy reading plays and this novalization still has a play feel about it more than a novel. I enjoyed it very much as a quick read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_521281810" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521281810" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5267338-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302795269p2/5267338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/521281810?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/5267338-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062006776" href="/book/show/9143175-the-unexpected-guest">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer521281810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3596770957025986524">So this was originally a play and adapted to a novel format. I did notice that the writing was a bit "off" and didn't feel quite right for an Agatha Christie book. The plot and characters were pretty interesting, as usual, starting off with pretty-clear case of wife being caught red-handed and holding the smoking gun. And in typical Christie style all is not what it appears to be. Not sure if it is because I've read so many of her books, but it didn't take me too long to figure out what the plot</span>
  <span id="freeText3596770957025986524" style="display:none">So this was originally a play and adapted to a novel format. I did notice that the writing was a bit "off" and didn't feel quite right for an Agatha Christie book. The plot and characters were pretty interesting, as usual, starting off with pretty-clear case of wife being caught red-handed and holding the smoking gun. And in typical Christie style all is not what it appears to be. Not sure if it is because I've read so many of her books, but it didn't take me too long to figure out what the plot-twist would be and who did it and why. Perhaps seeing it in a play may have kept me guessing a little longer. Overall, it was still a good read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3596770957025986524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2023658044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023658044" />
    <a title="Rose A" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49767093-rose-a"><img alt="Rose A" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449406114p2/49767093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2023658044?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose A" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose A" href="/user/show/49767093-rose-a">Rose A</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023658044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7913076465519821530">Decent plot though I could tell what the twist would be a mile away. While this is a decent novelisation, it feels very much like a play and I think would work better as such. Still, it contains Christie's excellent characterisation and understanding of psychology.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UbWLWIE3S1VojFwphHFVa8lUaJ+xaSBSpfs+uP8pD+PvtpQKzOBPE+rd9EVOnC8CEAcXtFaNiPKXxZlqkBLq3w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EnTj6WaYu57ct0hipZbst/BGOU2GWmlmLfAXP02LDfusd/y7K0+/2F7m4A5ve5beKRVGZmG+wcYfzrDtIrDoxw==')})
  }

For the very first time, this book prints Agatha\'s original ending, painstakingly transcribed from the hand-written draft in one of her earliest notebooks.\n\nEvery decade saw Agatha Christie\'s success grow to new heights. The emergence of the world-famous Collins Crime Club in 1930 brought with it the very first Miss Marple novel; the austerity of the 1940s had Agatha Christie preparing to kill off Hercule Poirot; and the 1950s saw her experiment increasingly with stories influenced by more modern thrillers. Focusing on more than 20 Christie novels as detailed evidence, John Curran demonstrates the evolution of Agatha\'s writing through the decades, including her perseverance through the Swinging Sixties and Seventies into old age, concluding with a look at Agatha\'s last notebook and her ideas for an unwritten final book.\n\nAs well as revealing more than a dozen unpublished book ideas, \'Agatha Christie\'s Murder in the Making\' contains two new short stories from her archives - \'The Man Who Knew\' and an early Miss Marple draft, \'The Case of the Caretaker\'s Wife\'.\n\nNB: The first edition, first printing, has the ISBN on the reverse of the title page as in this record of the book but the back of the dust wrapper carries a different ISBN - 9780007908561! Sayers, and 10 other crime writers from the newly formed Detection Club collaborated in publishing a unique crime novel. In a literary game of consequences, each author would write one chapter, leaving G.K. Chesterton to write a typically paradoxical prologue and Anthony Berkeley to tie up all the loose ends. In addition, all of the authors provided their own solutions in sealed envelopes, all of which appeared at the end of the book, with Agatha Christie\'s ingenious conclusion acknowledged at the time to be \'enough to make the book worth buying on its own\'.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">About Agatha Christie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1589991473p3/123715.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">Agatha Christie
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
42,810
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2103964310061385484"><i>Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16273767.Mary_Westmacott' title='Mary Westmacott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary Westmacott</a></b>, and was occasionally published under the name <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19960421.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan' title='Agatha Christie Mallowan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie Mallowan</a></b>.</i><br/><br/>Agatha Christie is the best-selling author of all time. She wrote 66 crime novels and story collections, fourteen plays, and six novels under a pseudonym in Romance. Her books have sold over a billion copies in the English language and a billion in t</span>
  <span id="freeText2103964310061385484" style="display:none"><i>Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16273767.Mary_Westmacott" title="Mary Westmacott" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Westmacott</a></b>, and was occasionally published under the name <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19960421.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan" title="Agatha Christie Mallowan" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie Mallowan</a></b>.</i><br /><br />Agatha Christie is the best-selling author of all time. She wrote 66 crime novels and story collections, fourteen plays, and six novels under a pseudonym in Romance. Her books have sold over a billion copies in the English language and a billion in translation. According to Index Translationum, she remains the most-translated individual author, having been translated into at least 103 languages. She is the creator of two of the most enduring figures in crime literature-Hercule Poirot and Miss Jane Marple-and author of <i>The Mousetrap</i>, the longest-running play in the history of modern theatre. <br /><br />Agatha Mary Clarissa Miller was born in Torquay, Devon, England, U.K., as the youngest of three. The Millers had two other children: Margaret Frary Miller (1879–1950), called Madge, who was eleven years Agatha's senior, and Louis Montant Miller (1880–1929), called Monty, ten years older than Agatha. <br /><br />Before marrying and starting a family in London, she had served in a Devon hospital during the First World War, tending to troops coming back from the trenches. During the First World War, she worked at a hospital as a nurse; later working at a hospital pharmacy, a job that influenced her work, as many of the murders in her books are carried out with poison. During the Second World War, she worked as a pharmacy assistant at University College Hospital, London, acquiring a good knowledge of poisons which feature in many of her novels.<br /><br />Her first novel, <i>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</i>, came out in 1920. During her first marriage, Agatha published six novels, a collection of short stories, and a number of short stories in magazines.<br /><br />In late 1926, Agatha's husband, Archie, revealed that he was in love with another woman, Nancy Neele, and wanted a divorce. On 8 December 1926 the couple quarreled, and Archie Christie left their house, Styles, in Sunningdale, Berkshire, to spend the weekend with his mistress at Godalming, Surrey. That same evening Agatha disappeared from her home, leaving behind a letter for her secretary saying that she was going to Yorkshire. Her disappearance caused an outcry from the public, many of whom were admirers of her novels. Despite a massive manhunt, she was not found for eleven days.<br /><br />In 1930, Christie married archaeologist Max Mallowan (Sir Max from 1968) after joining him in an archaeological dig. Their marriage was especially happy in the early years and remained so until Christie's death in 1976.<br /><br />Christie frequently used familiar settings for her stories. Christie's travels with Mallowan contributed background to several of her novels set in the Middle East. Other novels (such as <i>And Then There Were None</i>) were set in and around Torquay, where she was born. Christie's 1934 novel <i>Murder on the Orient Express</i> was written in the Hotel Pera Palace in Istanbul, Turkey, the southern terminus of the railway. The hotel maintains Christie's room as a memorial to the author. The Greenway Estate in Devon, acquired by the couple as a summer residence in 1938, is now in the care of the National Trust.<br /><br />Christie often stayed at Abney Hall in Cheshire, which was owned by her brother-in-law, James Watts. She based at least two of her stories on the hall: the short story <i>The Adventure of the Christmas Pudding</i>, and the novel <i>After the Funeral</i>. Abney Hall became Agatha's greatest inspiration for country-house life, with all the servants and grandeur which have been woven into her plots.<br /><br /><br />To honour her many literary works, she was appointed Commander of the Order of the British Empire in the 1956 New Year Honours. The next year, she became the President of the Detection Club. <br /><br /><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agatha_Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia entry for Agatha Christie</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2103964310061385484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
